                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <span>
                          Cured
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="https://www.yahoo.com/food/tagged/fish" target="_blank">
                           salmon
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          may seem like one of those foods that is impossible to execute at home, but it is surprisingly simple, not to mention delicious. Here, Gramercy Tavern chef Michael Anthony shows us how to infuse a fillet with aromatic spices and fresh citrus. Its just the thing for a holiday brunch.
                         </span>

Hamilton. (Photo: Lowcountry Digital History Initiative.)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn April 1865, one of Charleston&#x2019;s most prominent chefs held a dinner to celebrate the end of the Civil War. According to published reports, toasts were made, lavish dishes were served, and songs were sung about President Abraham Lincoln and freedom. The chef was Nat Fuller, a celebrated culinary personality and recently freed slave. Prior to that evening, his guests had never dined together; they were black and white residents of Charleston, assembled by Fuller in the spirit of reconciliation.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis meal was recreated in Charleston this past April, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2015\u002F04\u002F08\u002Fus\u002Fsouth-carolina-officer-is-charged-with-murder-in-black-mans-death.html?_r=0\"\u003Efollowing the shooting of Walter Scott \u003C\u002Fa\u003Ethat shook the city and became part of the larger national conversation about violence, policing, and race relations. This second reconciliation dinner was meant to once again bring black and white Charlestonians to the same table, but it had another purpose &#x2014; to pay tribute to an African-American chef whose contributions had been long forgotten.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe dinner and Chef Fuller are the subject of the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.southernfoodways.org\u002Fgravy\u002Fa-charleston-feast-for-reconciliation-gravy-ep-17\u002F\"\u003Ecurrent podcast from the Southern Foodways Alliance\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, the organization dedicated to documenting the &#x201C;diverse food cultures of the changing American South.&#x201D; Philip Graitcer, a producer on the Gravy podcast series, traces the origin of the event, past and present, and talks to David Shields, the historian who has been piecing together Fuller&#x2019;s story.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F75a41e28d0e36406abfc46c93a5ebc0b54e03514.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EProfessor&#xA0;David Shields (Photo: Southern Foodways Alliance)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EShields is an English professor at the University of South Carolina, but his passion is Southern food. (His new book is called \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.amazon.com\u002FSouthern-Provisions-Creation-Revival-Cuisine\u002Fdp\u002F022614111X\"\u003E&#x201C;Southern Provisions: The Creation and Revival of a Cuisine.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) He learned about Fuller and dug deeper. Fuller&#x2019;s name had been lost to history, but his impact on the culinary scene of Civil War-era Charleston was significant. &#x201C;His story is a remarkable one on several fronts,&#x201D; said Shields. While Fuller was still enslaved, he was the city&#x2019;s most successful purveyor of game; he became one of the city&#x2019;s leading caterers; and he ran a popular restaurant called The Bachelor&#x2019;s Retreat. (At the time, certain slaves could operate businesses with the permission of their masters, who would take a cut of the proceeds.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EInterestingly, the dishes that Fuller specialized in were not the Southern staples celebrated today. It wasn&#x2019;t until years later that fried chicken, grits, biscuits, and the like would come to represent the region. Fuller was a classically trained chef and served the cosmopolitan cuisine preferred by the upper class of Charleston society. A newspaper ad for The Bachelor&#x2019;s Retreat promoted &#x201C;oyster and calf head soups, turkey, wild duck, roast beef, a la mode beef, roast lamb, chicken pie, oyster pie, vegetables, and dessert courses&#x201D; as menu options. Fuller even had flair with cocktails. The \u003Ci\u003EDaily Constitutionalist\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, a local newspaper, wrote about his Brandy Smash and went so far as to call him a &#x201C;renowned genius.&#x201D; &#x201C;Nat Fuller &#x2026; has a cunning way of fixing up water so as to take all the bad taste out of it,&#x201D; read the article. &#x201C;We did not get the exact receipt, but believe that ice, brandy, mint and sugar are some of the condiments used.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFuller was a free man for just a year and a half, having died of typhoid fever at the end of 1866. For those interested in Fuller&#x2019;s life and career, Shields has published \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fldhi.library.cofc.edu\u002Fexhibits\u002Fshow\u002Fnat_fuller\"\u003Ea longer biography on the Lowcountry Digital History Initiative website.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fa6464246ce2dcb33c8f1d336fd15315491dd9070.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EChef Kevin Mitchell. (Photo: Southern Foodways Alliance)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe site also features \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fldhi.library.cofc.edu\u002Fexhibits\u002Fshow\u002Fnat_fuller\u002Fa-chef---s-take--nat-fuller---\"\u003Ean appreciation of Fuller by Chef Kevin Mitchell\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, an instructor at the Culinary Institute of Charleston. He oversaw the menu for the 2015 reconciliation dinner and was joined in the kitchen by other local culinary talents, including Benjamin &#x201C;BJ&#x201D; Dennis, a noted \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.gullahgeecheecorridor.org\"\u003EGullah Geechee\u003C\u002Fa\u003E chef from the region, and Sean Brock of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.huskrestaurant.com\"\u003EHusk\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The first part of the evening took place in the same building that once housed The Bachelor&#x2019;s Retreat. After cocktails and hors d&#x2019;oeuvres, the 80 guests walked to \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fmccradysrestaurant.com\"\u003EMcCrady&#x2019;s\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlestoncitypaper.com\u002FEat\u002Farchives\u002F2015\u002F03\u002F19\u002Fhistoric-nat-fuller-dinner-menu-released\"\u003Erestaurant for dinner\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. It was an optimistic evening, with no foreshadowing of the awful event to come only two months later: On the night of June 17, one of the dinner&#x2019;s participants, state Senator Clementa C. Pinckney, would be \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnews.yahoo.com\u002Fracist-manifesto-linked-charleston-shooting-suspect-003222552.html\"\u003Eslain along with eight other members of his church\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in a brutal murder that shocked the country and changed Charleston and perhaps the South forever.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fe52a0886a722df67312709a96acbe9ada57d10ac.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EDessert is served. (Photo: Southern Foodways Alliance)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Pinckney believed, like Fuller believed, that racism is based on mediated images and on a lack of personal face-to-face knowledge of the circumstances and situations of other people,&#x201D; said Shields. &#x201C;When you get people at the same table talking to one another, that&#x2019;s the way you gain knowledge.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EShields continues to hold out hope for &#x201C;the possibility of a future where the friendship at the table is extended into society at large.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore on Southern cuisine from Yahoo Food:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Fthis-couple-quit-their-full-time-jobs-to-sell-124004469096.html\"\u003EThis couple quit their full-time jobs to sell farm-fresh peaches\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Fmeet-two-of-nashvilles-indie-brewers-100759877203.html\"\u003EMeet two of To celebrate today we present to you the ultimate French dessert &#x2014; layer upon layer of cr&#xEA;pes filled with creamy ricotta and sweet dulce de leche. The cake belongs to dreamy Swedish blogger Linda Lomelino and her stunning baking site&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcall-me-cupcake.blogspot.com.au\u002F\"\u003ECall Me Cupcake\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Her photographs are beautifully styled, airy, and every shot contains fresh flowers. Her pink Neapolitan cake was one of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Fcakes-of-the-day-2014-c1419970930549\u002Fphoto-neapolitan-cake-photo-1419974813055.html\"\u003EYahoo Food&#x2019;s Best Cakes of 2014\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Today she&#x2019;s back with a stunning cr&#xEA;pe cake.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I have a love\u002Fhate relationship with dulce de leche. It&#x2019;s deliciousness is kind of deceiving,&#x201D; she says about the caramelized milk used in cr&#xEA;pes. &#x201C;After a while, the dulce de leche turned into a sauce and was running down the sides. I still wanted to share this recipe though because it is truly delicious, albeit somewhat messy.&#x201C;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELomelino makes a cr&#xEA;pe batter and fries the thin pancakes in a small pan. She piles them on top of each other with parchment paper between each layer to ensure they don&#x2019;t stick. She then assembles the cake by taking one pancake and spreading a mixture made of ricotta cheese, powdered sugar and lemon zest. The next one gets a coating of dulce de leche and is layered on the previous pancake. She repeats this until she&#x2019;s left with a tower of cr&#xEA;pes before finishing it off with fresh berries and a dusting of powdered sugar. Serve this with your favorite coffee and bon&#xA0;app&#xE9;tit!&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EGet the recipe: \u003Ca Well, weve got a few more to add to the list, perfect to enjoy in the height of summer.","body":"\u003Cp\u003EHow&#x2019;s your cocktail bucket list coming along?\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBy now, you&#x2019;ve hopefully started chipping away at some of the traditional classics, like the Old Fashioned and Manhattan. Well, we&#x2019;ve got a few more to add to the list&#x2014;and right in time for summer.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETiki cocktails aren&#x2019;t a new fabrication. They&#x2019;ve been around as an official category of cocktails since the 1930s. And while they may now remind you of Caribbean resorts and kitschy bars, many of the most famous Polynesian potions were born in California, thanks to the original tiki masters \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fliquor.com\u002Farticles\u002Ftiki-cocktail-facts\u002F\"\u003EDonn Beach and Victor Bergeron\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and were made without artificial sweeteners.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen made correctly, these elixirs are as good as any cocktail made by super old-time bartenders like Jerry Thomas&#x2014;especially when you consider the unusual glassware and over-the-top adornments. Go on, take a trip to paradise with the five tiki cocktails you have to try before you die.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003E1.&#xA0;MAI TAI\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fed54481b3283ef7a36cec35a49904914b5e2385a.jpg\" alt=\"5 Classic Tiki Cocktails to Drink Before You Die\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s not known who exactly invented this drink. Some say it was dreamt up by tiki pioneer Victor Bergeron in 1944; others say it was the father of tiki, Donn Beach. Sure, the Mai Tai can be a little sweet, but that&#x2019;s only to offset the flavors of aged rum, lime juice and orgeat. A great Mai Tai is far from cloying and a must-try for any tiki enthusiast.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fliquor.com\u002Frecipes\u002Ftraditional-mai-tai\u002F\"\u003EGet the recipe for the Mai Tai.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003E2.&#xA0;FOG CUTTER\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F991f9915ae929b4758e23ef091d6f7f91053fd08.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFeeling a little under the weather? Perhaps you&#x2019;re trying to push off last night&#x2019;s hangover? Fortunately for you, the Fog Cutter is true to its name. It&#x2019;s also not clear who invented this tried-and-true tropical concoction, but the mixture of rum, brandy, citrus juices, orgeat and sherry is both unexpected (sherry and brandy in a tiki cocktail?) and unforgettable.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fdrinkwire.liquor.com\u002Fpost\u002Flemonade-with-an-attitude-the-fog-cutter\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EGet the recipe for the Fog Cutter.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003E3.&#xA0;BERMUDA RUM SWIZZLE\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F8f6c8c12a4521638edf848fec6094301f6bf8087.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOften called the unofficial national drink of Bermuda, the Rum Swizzle predates both Donn Beach and Victor Bergeron. Its history, however, is still murky. Likely invented somewhere in the Caribbean, this mixture of black and gold rums, orange and pineapple juices, grenadine and Angostura bitters is as tropical and refreshing as a cool ocean breeze on a steamy beach day.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fliquor.com\u002Frecipes\u002Fbermuda-rum-swizzle\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EGet the recipe for the Bermuda Rum Swizzle.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003E4.&#xA0;PI&#xD1;A COLADA\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"528\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F3ec20238662cc735ff8b2fb6dda06804475c8ff2.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf there&#x2019;s one cocktail on this list you&#x2019;ve probably tried already, there&#x2019;s a good chance it&#x2019;s the classic, blended Pi&#xF1;a Colada. The tropical cocktail is made with a super-simple blend of rum, pineapple and coconut milk. It&#x2019;s enough to transport you to paradise&#x2014;but, honestly, there&#x2019;s no need to get caught in the rain.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fliquor.com\u002Frecipes\u002Fpina-colada\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EGet the recipe for the Pi&#xF1;a Colada.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003E5.&#xA0;PAINKILLER\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"400\" height=\"400\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w400\u002Fcfe6d92b6992238f1048ebd4d722f95c660fdaaa.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s true: A few of these cocktails and all your pains will drift away. This four-ingredient twist on the traditional Pi&#xF1;a Colada comprises rum, pineapple and orange juices and cream of coconut. Fruity, yes, but the juice is handily fresh-squeezed. Avocado Soup Recipe From Chocolate &amp; Marrow","summary":"Brooke Conroy Bass of Chocolate &amp; Marrowwalks us through a recipe forsopa fra de aguacate, a chilled avocado soup of Mexican origin.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EEvery week, we&#x2019;re \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Ftagged\u002Fblogger-of-the-week\"\u003Espotlighting a different food blogger\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;who&#x2019;s shaking up the blogosphere with tempting recipes and knockout photography. Below, Brooke Conroy Bass of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fchocolateandmarrow.com\u002F\"\u003EChocolate &amp; Marrow\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;walks us through a recipe for&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003Esopa fr&#xED;a de aguacate, a chilled avocado soup of Mexican origin.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F8c77f5e5e03861a89121b85803fb1dc02190aa4a.jpg\" alt=\"Chilled Avocado Soup Recipe From &#x2018;Chocolate &amp; Marrow&#x2019;\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPhoto: Brooke Conroy Bass\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESopa Fr&#xED;a de Aguacate, 2 Ways\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EServes 6-8\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EFor a food blogger, summertime is all about grilling fresh vegetables and meats &#x2014; embracing the beautiful weather and the bounty of produce that surrounds us. But you know what sucks about that? The dearth of soup! Recently I decided to try my hand at something I&#x2019;d never done before &#x2014; a chilled soup, utilizing seasonal ingredients like avocados, chiles, and tomatoes.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe dish is a Mexican soup called sopa fr&#xED;a de aguacate, or chilled avocado soup. The way I&#x2019;ve prepared it here is not vegetarian, though it easily could be adapted to fit a vegetarian lifestyle as I describe in the recipe. As I was making this soup, though, I felt torn &#x2014; do I prepare it in its classic form or try something a little less traditional? But then I thought, why the heck is there an &#x201C;or&#x201D; in that sentence? Why not just do both?\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ESo both I did, making the first the classic way by topping it with a trio of tomatoes, onions, and jalepenos. The second I topped with lump crabmeat and an extra hit of cayenne. Both were bright, refreshing, and fresh, but you could honestly top this soup with just about anything.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E4 jalape&#xF1;o chiles, divided (3 jalape&#xF1;o stemmed, seeded, and chopped roughly; the remaining jalape&#xF1;o stemmed, seeded, and chopped finely for topping)\u003Cbr\u003E3 large ripe avocados, pitted, peeled, and chopped into chunks\u003Cbr\u003E1 medium white onion, divided into 2 parts (chop half roughly and the other half finely for optional topping)\u003Cbr\u003E6 cups chicken stock (or vegetable stock for a vegetarian alternative)\u003Cbr\u003E&#xBC; cup cream (optional)\u003Cbr\u003EJuice of &#xBD; a lime\u003Cbr\u003E&#xBD; teaspoon of cayenne pepper, plus more if desired\u003Cbr\u003ESalt, to taste\u003Cbr\u003E&#xBD; cup of lump crabmeat for topping (optional)\u003Cbr\u003E2 plum tomatoes, cored, seeded, and finely chopped (optional)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBegin by pur&#xE9;eing the 3 stemmed jalape&#xF1;os, the avocados, and &#xBD; of the onion until a thick paste forms. Add to a large pot with the chicken stock, cream, and lime juice. Use an immersion blender to blend until silky smooth. (Alternatively, you could combine all of these ingredients in a large food processor and blend it all there. If you do this, you may need to pass it through a fine strainer to get the larger chunks out.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESeason soup with cayenne pepper and salt, to taste. Place in refrigerator for 1-2 hours, until chilled.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETop with lump crab meat and\u002For finely chopped onions, tomatoes, and remaining pepper just before serving.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ENotes: This recipe is easily made vegan by simply omitting the cream and crabmeat and substituting vegetable broth for the chicken broth.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore chilled things to slurp:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca Couple Quit Their Full-Time Jobs to Sell Farm-Fresh Peaches","summary":"When Stephen Rose was trying to persuade his Seattle-born girlfriend Jessica to move to Nashville, he convinced her of some of the South virtues: front porches, lakes and sweet, juicy peaches.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fd7e284263e046a136a35b5b5aa40650ad8b8c7c4.jpg\" alt=\"This Couple Quit Their Full-Time Jobs to Sell Farm-Fresh Peaches\" width=\"540\" height=\"521\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EStephen and Jessica Rose from The Peach Truck, (Photo: Lily Glass)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen Stephen Rose was trying to persuade his Seattle-born girlfriend Jessica to move to Nashville, he convinced her of some of the South virtues: front porches, lakes and sweet, juicy peaches.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe problem was once he moved, he couldn&#x2019;t find any.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETo solve what the couple dubbed &#x201C;the peach problem,&#x201D; Rose drove to Georgia, where he grew up, and picked a peach to show Jessica what all the fuss was about. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThey decided if they were willing to drive across state lines to get these peaches, other Nashville residents could become converts. The couple married, and when they got back from their honeymoon in the summer of 2012, they started selling from a truck peaches that had been picked the day before and driven over from Georgia.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"537\" height=\"810\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w537\u002Fea8aee0a47c9b0611093079b7a08057fafbe7268.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPhoto: Lily Glass\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThey also started knocking on the doors of restaurants, offering to supply them with Georgia peaches, from Pearson Farm, a fifth-generation peach farm run by a couple who were close family friends. Stephen and Jessica were so successful that the couple started seriously considering quitting their full-time jobs.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I felt like at 26, I was signing up for the rest of my life to this monotonous daily corporate grind,&#x201D; says Rose, who worked in corporate sales. &#x201C;We got to talking, and said what if we give up our summers &#x2014; and our summers are insane &#x2014; but literally have five months to do whatever we want to do.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBy the summer of 2013 they took the plunge. The business has now expanded to include 50 &#x201C;peach slingers&#x201D; who work across Nashville selling peaches for $8 for a 3-pound bag, a team of five who sell peaches throughout Kentucky, Tennessee, Ohio, and Indiana, and an \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthepeachtruck.com\u002Fproducts\u002Fpeach-box\"\u003EInternet-sales business\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. They now sell more than one million peaches a season.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"438\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F521b00c991ed2dc83a95c2d463e0b7cc993f1755.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPeaches packed for shipping; Photo: Jamie Clayton\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOne reason these are the best peaches you&#x2019;ll ever have, Rose boasts, is because the Peach Truck only focuses on one item, as opposed to grocery stores, which deal with thousands.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAlso, it&#x2019;s supply chain is much more direct. By the time a peach makes it into the hands of a grocery store customer, it&#x2019;s gone from the farm to a central distribution center, then onto a local center. Once it&#x2019;s in the grocery store, it sits in the back until they need to restock. That means weeks in between ripening on the tree and ending up on a buyer&#x2019;s hand.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe Peach Truck gets peaches that are picked in the morning, packed in the afternoon, and then put on a truck are ready for sale the next day. All that &#x201C;extra&#x201D; time on the tree makes a big difference in flavor.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhy are these peaches superior? Geography and climate play a huge roll in how a peach tastes, Rose says. Georgia soil is dense red clay that holds nutrients right below the surface. During the summer, heat can hover and 95 degrees and humid during the day &#x2014; and only getting down to about 80 degrees at night.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"354\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F52beb389bd41f862290aa273a80f3445fe361357.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EJessica and Stephen Rose talking with customers; Photo: Lily Glass\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It&#x2019;s miserably hot, and that peach is suffering, day and night,&#x201D; Rose says. &#x201C;But that suffering builds up that sugar content and you get that sweet, juicy peach you dream about.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EJosh Habiger, the chef at Pinewood Social and the culinary director for \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fstrategichospitalityonline.com\u002F\"\u003EStrategic Hospitality\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which operates a few Nashville restaurants including \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fthecatbirdseatrestaurant.com\u002F\"\u003EThe Catbird Seat\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, was one of the chefs that the Roses approached.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;This dude showed up one day, and says, &#x2018;Hey man, we drove our truck down and have some peaches and they were handing them out old-school style,&#x201D; Habiger says. &#x201C;Now, everyone in the restaurant business here is aware of the peach truck, everyone uses their peaches.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAt his restaurants, the peaches are making appearances in dishes like a peach and burrata salad at \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpinewoodsocial.com\u002F\"\u003EPinewood Social\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and oysters with a peach mignonette at the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.thepattersonnashville.com\u002F\"\u003EPatterson House\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Right now we&#x2019;re at the peak where peaches are just perfect,&#x201D; Habiger says. &#x201C;You take a bite and it just runs down your face.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFellow chef Sean Brock, who is behind \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.huskrestaurant.com\u002F\"\u003EHusk\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, the famed restaurant with locations in Charleston and Nashville came across the Peach Truck while at a farmers market.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I could smell the peaches a mile away,&#x201D; Brock says, and sought out the couple to learn more.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBrock liked that the peaches were produced in a way that preserved sustainable farming traditions from multiple generations. The farm isn&#x2019;t certified organic &#x2014; the humid southeast can make bugs a problem &#x2014; but pesticides are only used as a last-line of defense, and care is taken to make sure the soil is full of nutrients for next year&#x2019;s crop.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It&#x2019;s rare for peach farmers to follow old-fashioned and sustainable ways of raising them because it&#x2019;s very difficult,&#x201D; Brock says. &#x201C;But you can smell and taste the difference.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"403\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fd81187500cd91e038eccc1e567d53fd80025136c.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe peach crop now is a worry for Rose, because his growing family, which now includes a baby daughter, depends on it. He says they live more simply in order to have more free time in the off-season, and they also save up for the future because they don&#x2019;t know what the next growing season will look like. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd while several months off a year to travel sounds amazing &#x2014; and the Roses plan to take their daughter and travel through Spain, Portugal and Morocco &#x2014; the down time isn&#x2019;t all vacation. Rose has picked up other jobs, including driving for Uber, in the off-season.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe couple is also trying to make the most of this one and expand further afield. On Friday, the Roses are coming to New York City for stops at farmers and food markets.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E Rose can&#x2019;t wait to see New Yorkers&#x2019; reactions. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I&#x2019;ve seen people bite in and get tears in their eyes, and say, &#x2018;I remember when I was a kid and tasted peaches like this, and I haven&#x2019;t in years,&#x2019;&#x201D; Rose says. &#x201C;I think a lot of people in New York will have that same reaction and it&#x2019;s pretty thrilling.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECraving more peaches?
